## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: classical mechanics â€” nonlinear oscillations / dynamical systems
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is acceleration expressed as a function of position x, velocity v, and possibly time t, matching second-order ODE models of (nonlinear) oscillators with restoring forces, damping, and external/parametric forcing.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear harmonic oscillator (undamped, unforced): dv_dt = c0 * x (restoring acceleration proportional to displacement)
- Viscous damping oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear damping plus linear stiffness)
- Time-dependent stiffness (parametric system): dv_dt = (c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x + c3 * v (parametric excitation of stiffness)
- Periodically forced oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * cos(c3 * t) (external periodic drive)
- Duffing oscillator (cubic stiffness): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (hardening/softening spring nonlinearity)
- Duffing with periodic forcing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (nonlinear stiffness plus drive)
- Pendulum-like restoring force: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) + c2 * v (large-angle oscillations; sinusoidal restoring term)
- Quadratic (aerodynamic) damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * Abs(v) (drag proportional to speed squared)
- Nonlinear damping (cubic): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (amplitude-dependent dissipation)
- Van der Pol-type self-excited oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (c2 - x**2) * v (negative damping at small |x|, positive at large |x|)
- Rayleigh-type self-excited oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + (c1 - c2 * v**2) * v (velocity-dependent pumping leading to limit cycles)
- Nonlinear coupling (mixed term): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * x**2 * v (state-dependent damping/coupling)
- Polynomial potential (energy-based) model: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 + c3 * v (higher-order restoring force from a nonlinear potential)
- Quasi-periodic/multi-harmonic forcing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * cos(c3 * t) + c4 * cos(c5 * t) (multiple drive frequencies)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope â†’ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects â†’ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay â†’ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior â†’ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects â†’ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Conservative restoring dynamics often appear as dv_dt depending only on x (no v term) and commonly as an odd function in x (e.g., c0*x, c0*sin(c1*x), c0*x + c1*x**3).
- Linear dissipation is indicated by an additive term proportional to v; the coefficient sign determines damping vs. pumping.
- Amplitude-dependent frequency shifts (hardening/softening behavior) are commonly captured by adding x**3 (Duffing) or higher odd powers of x to the restoring term.
- Self-sustained (limit-cycle) oscillations are typically modeled by a damping term that changes sign with state magnitude, e.g., (c0 - x**2)*v or (c0 - v**2)*v.
- Quadratic drag or turbulent dissipation is suggested by v*Abs(v) (or similar odd-in-v nonlinearities) rather than a purely linear v term.
- External periodic forcing usually manifests as additive sin/cos terms in t that do not multiply x (direct forcing).
- Parametric excitation (time-varying stiffness) is suggested when periodic functions of t multiply x, e.g., cos(c*t)*x, which can produce resonance bands.
- If dv_dt has no explicit t dependence and damping is absent (no v terms), the system is often near energy-conserving; adding v terms breaks conservation and introduces decay/growth of amplitude.
- State-dependent dissipation/coupling often appears via mixed terms like x*v, x**2*v, or x*v*Abs(v), indicating damping strength depends on displacement.

GT: -c0*beta*v - mu*(c1 - v**c2)*v - omega0**c3*(gamma*Abs(v)**c4 + c5)*x
Candidates evaluated: 50

I need to analyze the Ground Truth (GT) expression and compare each candidate to it.

## Ground Truth Analysis

The GT numerical expression is:
$$-0.721004v(1 - v^2) - 1.03737v - 2.44077x(0.015413|v|^{1/3} + 1)$$

Expanding:
$$-0.721004v + 0.721004v^3 - 1.03737v - 2.44077x \cdot 0.015413|v|^{1/3} - 2.44077x$$

$$= -2.44077x + 0.721004v^3 - 1.75837v - 0.037622x|v|^{1/3}$$

So the GT has these terms:
1. **cآ·x** (linear in x)
2. **cآ·vآ³** (cubic in v)
3. **cآ·v** (linear in v)
4. **cآ·xآ·|v|^{1/3}** (x times |v|^{1/3})

Key: The term `|v|^{1/3}` involves the **absolute value** of v raised to 1/3. This is critical since v takes both positive and negative values.

Now let me check each candidate. I need candidates that can produce exactly these 4 basis functions: x, vآ³, v, and xآ·|v|^{1/3}.

The critical issue is whether candidates have `v^c` (which for fractional c and negative v is problematic/complex) vs `|v|^c` or `Abs(v)^c`. Let me check which candidates could match.

**Important note about `v**c4` terms:** When v can be negative and c4 is fractional (like 1/3), `v**c4` is not the same as `|v|^{c4}`. The GT explicitly uses `Abs(v)^{1/3}`. So candidates with `v**c4*x` where c4 would need to be 1/3 would NOT match because `v^{1/3}` â‰  `|v|^{1/3}` for negative v.

Let me systematically go through candidates, looking for those that:
- Have the right basis functions: x, vآ³, v, xآ·|v|^{1/3}
- Can eliminate unwanted terms (by setting coefficients to 0)
- Handle the |v| issue correctly

For candidates with terms like `v**c4*x`: this gives `v^{c4} \cdot x`, which for c4=1/3 gives `v^{1/3} \cdot x`. But for negative v, `v^{1/3}` is real (cube root of negative is negative), while `|v|^{1/3}` is always positive. So `v^{1/3} = \text{sign}(v) \cdot |v|^{1/3}`, which is NOT the same as `|v|^{1/3}`.

**This means NO candidate with `v**c*x` (fractional c) can match the GT's `|v|^{1/3}*x` term**, unless there are two such terms that could combine to produce `|v|^{1/3}`.

Wait - can two terms like `c3*v^{c4}*x + c5*v^{c6}*x` combine? If c4=1/3 and c6=1/3, they just add. We need `|v|^{1/3} = v^{1/3} \cdot \text{sign}(v)^{1/3}`... Actually for real-valued computation, `|v|^{1/3}` cannot be written as a finite sum of `v^{a_i}` terms.

Since `|v|^{1/3}` is an even-like function (always positive) while `v^{1/3}` is odd, they are fundamentally different. No combination of `v^c` terms can produce `|v|^c` for all v (positive and negative).

**Therefore, none of the candidates can match the GT**, because they all use `v**c` rather than `Abs(v)**c`, and the GT requires `Abs(v)^{1/3}` which behaves differently for negative v.

Let me verify: every single candidate uses `v**c4*x` or similar power-of-v terms, never `Abs(v)`. This confirms no match.
